### Key fix categories

- **Agent registry** — soft-delete with `deletedAt` timestamp instead of permanent removal; name reuse after deletion; `listAgents(includeDeleted)` parameter; AMP index cache invalidation on mutations
- **Memory system** — CozoDB schema migration (adds `indexed_at` column); consolidation dedup via `DISTINCT`; delta indexing `maxAge` guard; embedding dimension validation
- **Terminal** — WebGL addon error handling; scrollback history timeout increase; tmux pane capture escaping
- **Wake route** — removed broken `RESUME_PATTERNS`/`stripResumeFlags()` (programs handle missing sessions gracefully)
- **AMP messaging** — `fromLabel`/`toLabel` population via registry lookup; signature/public key preservation in `convertAMPToMessage()`
- **Shell scripts** — SC2086 quoting fixes in `install.sh`, `update-aimaestro.sh`, `remote-install.sh`, `install-messaging.sh`; `-y` flag support in `install-hooks.sh`; idempotent re-run guards in installers
- **Delete UX** — confirmation dialog with typed agent name; soft-delete API with `?permanent=true` option
- **Types** — removed 6 dead/unused interfaces from `types/agent.ts`; cleaned up `types/marketplace.ts`
- **Tests** — 91 agent registry tests (including soft-delete, rename, name reuse); all 281 tests pass
- **Skills & scripts** (plugin submodule) — updated 6 SKILL.md files + `aimaestro-agent.sh` fixes (see [ai-maestro-plugins#1](https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins/pull/1)

Here's where everything lives right now:

**Current location of all fixes:**

| Repo | Branch | Status |
|------|--------|--------|
| `ai-maestro` (main repo) | `fix/aim-222-all-fixes` | PR #206 open, not merged to `main` |
| `ai-maestro-plugins` (submodule) | `fix/aim-222-skills-scripts` | PR #1 open, not merged to `main` |

You're currently **on** `fix/aim-222-all-fixes` — so your working tree already has all the fixes. They just haven't been merged into `main` yet.

**Two ways to get them on your local `main`:**

### Option A: Merge the PRs on GitHub first (recommended)

1. Merge [ai-maestro-plugins#1](https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins/pull/1) first (so the submodule pointer resolves)
2. Merge [ai-maestro#206](https://github.com/23blocks-OS/ai-maestro/pull/206)
3. Then locally:
```bash
git checkout main
git pull origin main
git submodule update --init
```

### Option B: Merge locally right now (skip GitHub review)

```bash
git checkout main
git merge fix/aim-222-all-fixes
git submodule update --init
```

This gives you everything on local `main` immediately. You can still merge the GitHub PRs later to keep the remote in sync.

Which approach do you prefer?

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:32:30]*

Yes. The consolidated branch includes commit `97d94be` which updates the submodule pointer to `0759e09` — the commit with all skill/script fixes. After `git submodule update --init`, your local `plugin/` directory will be at that commit with all the fixes.

The GitHub PR on the plugins repo (#1) is only about merging those changes into the **upstream** `main` of `23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins`. Locally, Option B gives you everything.

One caveat: the submodule remote likely points to `23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins`. Commit `0759e09` exists there (GitHub stores fork PR commits on the upstream), but if `git submodule update` can't fetch it, you'd need to add the fork remote inside the submodule:

```bash
cd plugin
git remote add fork https://github.com/Emasoft/ai-maestro-plugins.git
git fetch fork
cd ..
git submodule update --init
```

That should only be needed if the fetch fails. In most cases `git submodule update --init` will just work.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:33:53]*


## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:34:07]*


## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:34:08]*

You're right to question that. It almost certainly won't fail. GitHub supports fetching commits by SHA even when they're only in PR refs, and modern git (2.20+) uses that capability. The commit `0759e09` exists on GitHub's storage for `23blocks-OS/ai-maestro-plugins` (via the PR), so `git submodule update --init` will find it.

The caveat was unnecessary. Option B is straightforward:

```bash
git checkout main
git merge fix/aim-222-all-fixes
git submodule update --init
```

That's it.

     1→/**
     2→ * CozoDB Schema for Long-Term Memory
     3→ *
     4→ * Implements a biological memory model:
     5→ * - Short-term: Current RAG system (messages, msg_vec, msg_terms)
     6→ * - Warm: Recently consolidated, frequently accessed
     7→ * - Long-term: Permanent, distilled knowledge
     8→ *
     9→ * Inspired by:
    10→ * - Claude-Cognitive: HOT/WARM/COLD tiers
    11→ * - Cipher: System 1/2 separation (knowledge vs reasoning)
    12→ * - Cognee: Graph relationships between memories
    13→ */
    14→
    15→import { AgentDatabase } from './cozo-db'

    17→

    19→ * Memory categories following System 1/2 model
    20→ */
    21→export type MemoryCategory =
    22→  | 'fact'        // System 1: Specific information (URLs, paths, names)
    23→  | 'decision'    // System 1: Choices made with rationale
    24→  | 'preference'  // System 1: User/project preferences
    25→  | 'pattern'     // System 2: Recurring workflows
    26→  | 'insight'     // System 2: Learned understanding
    27→  | 'reasoning'   // System 2: How problems were solved
    28→
    29→export type MemoryTier = 'warm' | 'long'
    30→export type MemorySystem = 1 | 2  // 1 = knowledge, 2 = reasoning
    31→
    32→export type RelationshipType =
    33→  | 'leads_to'    // This memory led to another
    34→  | 'contradicts' // This memory contradicts another
    35→  | 'supports'    // This memory supports another
    36→  | 'supersedes'  // This memory replaces another
    37→

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:41:59]*

I can see that `handleDeleteAgent` in `page.tsx` calls the API without `?hard=true`, which means it does a soft-delete. The DeleteAgentDialog says "Delete Forever" and "This action cannot be undone" which is misleading for a soft-delete. Let me note this as a UX inconsistency.

Now let me check the `fromLabel` and AMP `amp` field consistency in messageQueue.ts.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 21:43:13]*

Line 13: `isolatedModules: true`. With `isolatedModules`, you can still import an interface as a value import (without `type` keyword) in TypeScript - what `isolatedModules` prevents is re-exporting types. And since Next.js uses its own bundler, this import pattern is fine (Next.js transpiles with SWC/Babel which handles this). So this is not an actual issue.

   700→export function deleteAgent(id: string, hard: boolean = false): boolean {
   701→  const agents = loadAgents()

   213→export function getAgent(id: string, includeDeleted: boolean = false): Agent | null {
   214→  const agents = loadAgents()
   215→  const agent = agents.find(a => a.id === id) || null
   216→  // If the agent is soft-deleted and caller didn't ask for deleted agents, return null
   217→  if (agent && agent.deletedAt && !includeDeleted) return null
   218→  return agent
   219→}
   220→
   221→/**
   222→ * Get agent by name (the primary identity)
   223→ * Names are unique per-host, like email addresses (auth@macbook-pro ≠ auth@mac-mini)
   224→ *
   225→ * @param name - Agent name (case-insensitive)
   226→ * @param hostId - Optional host ID. If provided, searches on that host. If not, searches on self host.
   227→ */
   228→export function getAgentByName(name: string, hostId?: string): Agent | null {
   229→  const agents = loadAgents()
   230→  const normalizedName = name.toLowerCase()
   231→
   232→  if (hostId) {
   233→    // Scoped to specific host; exclude soft-deleted agents
   234→    return agents.find(a =>
   235→      !a.deletedAt &&
   236→      a.name?.toLowerCase() === normalizedName &&
   237→      a.hostId?.toLowerCase() === hostId.toLowerCase()
   238→    ) || null
   239→  }
   240→
   241→  // Default: search on self host only; exclude soft-deleted agents
   242→  const selfHostId = getSelfHostId().toLowerCase()
   243→  return agents.find(a =>
   244→    !a.deletedAt &&
   245→    a.name?.toLowerCase() === normalizedName &&
   246→    a.hostId?.toLowerCase() === selfHostId
   247→  ) || null
   248→}
   249→
   250→/**
   251→ * Get agent by name from ANY host (global search)
   252→ * Use sparingly - prefer getAgentByName(name, hostId) for per-host lookups
   253→ */
   254→export function getAgentByNameAnyHost(name: string): Agent | null {
   255→  const agents = loadAgents()
   256→  // Exclude soft-deleted agents from name lookups
   257→  return agents.find(a => !a.deletedAt && a.name?.toLowerCase() === name.toLowerCase()) || null

   388→        method: 'DELETE',
   389→      })
   390→
   391→      if (!response.ok) {
   392→        const data = await response.json()
   393→        throw new Error(data.error || 'Failed to delete agent')
   394→      }
   395→

   397→      setIsProfileOpen(false)
   398→      setProfileAgent(null)
   399→      setProfileScrollToDangerZone(false)
   400→

   402→      if (activeAgentId === agentId) {
   403→        setActiveAgentId(null)
   404→      }
   405→
   406→      // Refresh agents list
   407→      refreshAgents()
   408→
   409→      // Trigger subconscious status refresh
